Hierarchical clustering demo

Task: Show the relationship among European languages, given a Python dictionary that contains the frequencies of letters (and character n-grams) for the different European languages.

A Python dictionary has items. Each item has a key and a value. The keys are unique within the dictionary. The values can be of any type.

{key1:value1, key2:value2, ..., key_n:value_n}

Input: A dictionary that has been pickled/converted into a byte stream stored in a file 'letters.data', which you can download here. The keys are two letter codes identifying the languages (ISO 639-1); the values are the frequencies of letters (and character n-grams) for each of the languages. The frequency statistics were computed from the Europarl dataset, which contains the proceedings of the European Parliament in all the languages of the EU.

In [1]:
import pickle

from sklearn.feature_extraction import DictVectorizer
from sklearn.feature_extraction.text import TfidfTransformer
from sklearn.preprocessing import StandardScaler, FunctionTransformer, Normalizer
from sklearn.pipeline import make_pipeline

import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
%config InlineBackend.figure_format = 'svg' 
plt.style.use('seaborn')

import numpy as np
In [2]:
#Read a pickled object representation from the file letters.data and 
#return the original object 
#'rb' means reading bytes
with open('letters.data', 'rb') as f:
    letter_data = pickle.load(f)

#can also be written as follows:
#f = open('letters.data', 'rb')
#letter_data = pickle.load(f)

In [8]:
#Take only items whose keys are valid alphabet in European languages
def is_valid(s):
    if len(s) > 1:
        return False
    if not str.isalpha(s):
        return False
    return True


def clean_dict(d):
    return { k:v for k, v in d.items() if is_valid(k) }

X = [ clean_dict(letter_data[l]) for l in languages ]

pipeline = make_pipeline(
    DictVectorizer(),
    TfidfTransformer(),
    Normalizer(),
    FunctionTransformer(lambda x: x.todense(), accept_sparse=True),
    #StandardScaler(with_std=False)
)
Xv = pipeline.fit_transform(X)

In [13]:
# code borrowed from https://github.com/scikit-learn/scikit-learn/blob/70cf4a676caa2d2dad2e3f6e4478d64bcb0506f7/examples/cluster/plot_hierarchical_clustering_dendrogram.py

from scipy.cluster.hierarchy import dendrogram
from sklearn.cluster import AgglomerativeClustering

def plot_dendrogram(model, **kwargs):

    # Children of hierarchical clustering
    children = model.children_

    # Distances between each pair of children
    # Since we don't have this information, we can use a uniform one for plotting
    distance = np.arange(children.shape[0])

    # The number of observations contained in each cluster level
    no_of_observations = np.arange(2, children.shape[0]+2)

    # Create linkage matrix and then plot the dendrogram
    linkage_matrix = np.column_stack([children, distance, no_of_observations]).astype(float)

    # Plot the corresponding dendrogram
    dendrogram(linkage_matrix, **kwargs)

Below, we see how to carry out hierarchical clustering using scikit-learn's AgglomerativeClustering. We try out a few different ways to build the hierarchies.
